[1m(ูจ) ุงูุฃุตูุงุช ุงูุฃุฑุณุชูุฑุงุทูุฉ [0m

Most of the Roman historians wrote with aristocratic prejudices, but Ciceroโs [3mLetters to Atticus [0mgive a clear sense of what was at 
stake for the ruling orders in the republicโs last century. All well-educated nobles in later centuries knew them. A vivid picture 
of chivalric values in action is the epic of [3mTiran lo Blanc [0m, devoured as late as the 18th century by Catherine the Great. 
Castiglioneโs [3mThe Courtier [0mis the most important, and still very readable, handbook of aristocratic conduct. An English equivalent 
is Sir Thomas Elyotโs [3mThe Boke called the Governor [0m. Noble life under Louis XIV is elegantly chronicled in Mme de Sรฉvignรฉโs [3m
Letters [0m, while the world of his court is reported and commented upon in incomparable detail through the voluminous [3mMemoirs [0mof the 
Duke de Saint-Simon. Chesterfieldโs [3mLetters to His Son [0mprescribe how to be a gentleman in the 18th century, while Montesquieuโs 
contemporaneous [3mSpirit of the Laws [0mreflects on the whole of aristocratic history in elaborating new rationales for noble 
behaviour. The memoirs of Princess Dashkov record the life of the Russian elite, at home and abroad, under Catherine, and the 
first volume of Alexander Herzenโs describes a noble upbringing in early 19th-century Russia. The literary skill of Chateaubriand 
makes the memoirs he sold for posthumous publication a memorable romantic description of changing noble fortunes over the 
revolutionary and Napoleonic upheavals. The sad dissolution of the Irish Ascendancy is movingly portrayed in David Thompson, [3m
Woodbrook. [0mA trivial romp through what was left of noble ideals by the mid-20th century is Nancy Mitford (ed.), [3mNoblesse Oblige: 
An Enquiry into the Identifiable Characteristics of the English Aristocracy [0m(1956). 

[1m(ูฉ) ุงูุฃุฑุณุชูุฑุงุทูุฉ ูู ุงูุฃุฏุจ [0m

Cervantesโs [3mDon Quixote [0mis perhaps the best-known petty nobleman in literature, ridiculed and admired in equal measure. On the eve 
of the French Revolution, the heartlessness of nobles was unblinkingly depicted by Goethe in [3mThe Sorrows of Young Werther [0m, 
Choderlos de Laclos in [3mDangerous Liaisons [0m, or Beaumarchaisโs play [3mThe Marriage of Figaro [0m. Classic and timeless portrayals of the 
everyday values of gentlefolk are the novels of Jane Austen, particularly [3mPersuasion [0mand [3mMansfield Park [0m. The obsessional hunting 
of Anthony Trollope gave him much first-hand material for the pictures of the Victorian landed classes found throughout his vast 
output, but particularly in the Palliser novels. See also R. Gilmour, [3mThe Idea of the Gentleman in the Victorian [0mNovel (1981). The 
boredom of Russian noble life in the same century is amply chronicled, whether in Turgenevโs [3mA Nest of Gentlefolk [0m, Gogolโs [3mDead 
Souls [0m, or Goncharovโs [3mOblomov [0m. The equivalent for France are the elegiac novels of Marcel Proust. A somewhat fawning celebration 
of the exclusivism of English Catholic aristocrats in the 20th century was Evelyn Waughโs [3mBrideshead Revisited [0m, subsequently made 
into a sumptuous television series based on one of the greatest of country houses, Castle Howard. And one of the best-selling 
novels of that century was turned into a superb film by the aristocratic Marxist Luchino Visconti: Prince Giuseppe di Lampedusaโs [3m
The Leopard [0mis a marvellous portrait of a traditional Sicilian grandee confronted by the social and political challenges of the 
19th century.
